Bollinger was censoring the Band\'s speech.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Concerned alumni initiated an organized campaign to restore the Orgo Night show by publishing a series of pamphlets addressing the issues.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> University administration continued to prohibit the traditional Orgo Night performance during the spring semester of 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> prompting the Marching Band to again stage the show outside the library on May 4, 2017 as continued objections from alumni persist. University administrators sent a letter to concerned alumni on April 27, 2017 claiming to be "working closely" with the current Band leadership concerning the future of Orgo Night, but the statement turned out to be false. Band leadership had received no communications or outreach from the university and the administrators had refused to engage in any discussion about the future of the Orgo Night tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tree-Lighting_and_Yule_Log_ceremonies">Tree-Lighting and Yule Log ceremonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Tree-Lighting and Yule Log ceremonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Collegewalk2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Collegewalk2.jpg/220px-Collegewalk2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Collegewalk2.jpg/330px-Collegewalk2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Collegewalk2.jpg/440px-Collegewalk2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Collegewalk2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTree-Lighting at College Walk</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The campus Tree-Lighting Ceremony was inaugurated in 1998. It celebrates the illumination of the medium-sized trees lining College Walk in front of Kent and Hamilton Halls on the east end and Dodge and Journalism Halls on the west, just before finals week in early December. The lights remain on until February 28. Students meet at the sun-dial for free hot chocolate, performances by <i>a cappella</i> groups, and speeches by the university president and a guest.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Immediately following the College Walk festivities is one of Columbia\'s older holiday traditions, the lighting of the Yule Log. The Christmas ceremony dates to a period prior to the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, but lapsed before being revived by University President <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Murray_Butler" title="Nicholas Murray Butler">Nicholas Murray Butler</a> in the early 20th century. A troop of students dressed as <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">Continental Army</a> soldiers carry the eponymous log from the sun-dial to the lounge of John Jay Hall, where it is lit amid the singing of seasonal carols. The Christmas ceremony is accompanied by a reading of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Visit_From_St._Nicholas" class="mw-redirect" title="A Visit From St. Nicholas">A Visit From St. Nicholas</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Clement_Clarke_Moore" title="Clement Clarke Moore">Clement Clarke Moore</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Yes,_Virginia,_There_is_a_Santa_Claus" class="mw-redirect" title="Yes, Virginia, There is a Santa Claus">Yes, Virginia, There is a Santa Claus</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Francis_Pharcellus_Church" title="Francis Pharcellus Church">Francis Pharcellus Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Varsity_Show">The Varsity Show</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: The Varsity Show">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/The_Varsity_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="The Varsity Show">The Varsity Show</a> is an annual musical written by and for students and was established in 1894, making it one of Columbia\'s oldest traditions. Past writers and directors have included Columbians <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rodgers" title="Richard Rodgers">Richard Rodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Hammerstein_II" title="Oscar Hammerstein II">Oscar Hammerstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_Hart" title="Lorenz Hart">Lorenz Hart</a>, <a href="/wiki/I.A.L._Diamond" class="mw-redirect" title="I.A.L. Diamond">I.A.L. Diamond</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Herman_Wouk" title="Herman Wouk">Herman Wouk</a>. The show has one of the largest operating budgets of all university events.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Columbia_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Columbia_University_people" title="List of Columbia University people">List of Columbia University people</a></div>\n<p>As of 2011, Columbia alumni included three United States Presidents, 26 foreign Heads of State, ten Justices of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> (including three Chief Justices) and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">39 Nobel winners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> As of 2011, alumni also have received more than 35 <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="National Book Awards">National Book Awards</a> and 123 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prizes" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulitzer Prizes">Pulitzer Prizes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Columbia_University_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia_University-231">[231]</a></sup> Today,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2012)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> two <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Senator">United States Senators</a> and 16 Chief Executives of <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies hold Columbia degrees, as do three of the 25 richest Americans and 20 living billionaires.<sup id="cite_ref-Marie_Thibault_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marie_Thibault-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> Five <a href="/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States" title="Founding Fathers of the United States">Founding Fathers</a> including <a href="/wiki/Robert_R._Livingston_(chancellor)" title="Robert R. Livingston (chancellor)">a member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Five" title="Committee of Five">Committee of Five</a> are alumni of Columbia University, then named "King\'s College".<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[n 1]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Former U.S. Presidents <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin Delano Roosevelt">Franklin Delano Roosevelt</a> attended the law school. Other more recent political figures educated at Columbia include former U.S President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Associate_Justice_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Associate Justice of the Supreme Court of the United States">Associate Justice of the U.S. Supreme Court</a> <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Bader_Ginsburg" title="Ruth Bader Ginsburg">Ruth Bader Ginsburg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[239]</a></sup> former U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Madeleine_Albright" title="Madeleine Albright">Madeleine Albright</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[240]</a></sup> former chairman of the U.S. Federal Reserve Bank <a href="/wiki/Alan_Greenspan" title="Alan Greenspan">Alan Greenspan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[241]</a></sup> U.S. Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Eric_Holder" title="Eric Holder">Eric Holder</a>, and U.S. Solicitor General <a href="/wiki/Donald_Verrilli_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Donald Verrilli Jr.">Donald Verrilli Jr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[242]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> served as the thirteenth president of Columbia University from 1948 to 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[243]</a></sup> The university has also educated 26 foreign <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">heads of state</a>, including President of Georgia <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a>, President of East Timor <a href="/wiki/Jose_Ramos_Horta" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Ramos Horta">Jose Ramos Horta</a>, President of Estonia <a href="/wiki/Toomas_Hendrik_Ilves" title="Toomas Hendrik Ilves">Toomas Hendrik Ilves</a> and other historical figures such as <a href="/wiki/Wellington_Koo" title="Wellington Koo">Wellington Koo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radovan_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Radovan Karad\xc5\xbei\xc4\x87">Radovan Karad\xc5\xbei\xc4\x87</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaston_Eyskens" title="Gaston Eyskens">Gaston Eyskens</a>, and <a href="/wiki/T._V._Soong" title="T. V. Soong">T. V. Soong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[n 2]</a></sup> The author of India\'s constitution and <a href="/wiki/Dalit" title="Dalit">Dalit</a> leader Dr. <a href="/wiki/B._R._Ambedkar" title="B. R. Ambedkar">B. R. Ambedkar</a> was also an alumnus of Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[268]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Alumni of Columbia have occupied top positions in Wall Street and the rest of the business world. Notable members of the <a href="/wiki/Astor_family" title="Astor family">Astor family</a><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[270]</a></sup> attended Columbia, while some recent business graduates include investor <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[271]</a></sup> former CEO of PBS and NBC Larry Grossman,<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[272]</a></sup> and chairman of <a href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" class="mw-redirect" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a> <a href="/wiki/S._Robson_Walton" title="S. Robson Walton">S. Robson Walton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[273]</a></sup> CEO\'s of top Fortune 500 companies include <a href="/wiki/James_P._Gorman" title="James P. Gorman">James P. Gorman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[274]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_J._Stevens" title="Robert J. Stevens">Robert J. Stevens</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[275]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Dauman" title="Philippe Dauman">Philippe Dauman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Viacom" title="Viacom">Viacom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[276]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ursula_Burns" title="Ursula Burns">Ursula Burns</a> of <a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[277]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Vikram_Pandit" title="Vikram Pandit">Vikram Pandit</a> of <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[278]</a></sup> Notable labor organizer and women\'s educator <a href="/wiki/Louise_Leonard_McLaren" title="Louise Leonard McLaren">Louise Leonard McLaren</a> received her degree of Master of Arts from Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[279]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In science and technology, Columbia alumni include: founder of <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> <a href="/wiki/Herman_Hollerith" title="Herman Hollerith">Herman Hollerith</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[280]</a></sup> inventor of <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcast" class="mw-redirect" title="FM broadcast">FM radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Armstrong" class="mw-redirect" title="Edwin Armstrong">Edwin Armstrong</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[281]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Francis_Mechner" title="Francis Mechner">Francis Mechner</a>; integral in development of the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear submarine</a> <a href="/wiki/Hyman_G._Rickover" title="Hyman G. Rickover">Hyman Rickover</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[282]</a></sup> founder of <a href="/wiki/Google_China" title="Google China">Google China</a> <a href="/wiki/Kai-Fu_Lee" title="Kai-Fu Lee">Kai-Fu Lee</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[283]</a></sup> scientists <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Jay_Gould" title="Stephen Jay Gould">Stephen Jay Gould</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[284]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Millikan" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Millikan">Robert Millikan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[285]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Helium%E2%80%93neon_laser" title="Helium\xe2\x80\x93neon laser">Helium\xe2\x80\x93neon laser</a> inventor <a href="/wiki/Ali_Javan" title="Ali Javan">Ali Javan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mihajlo_Pupin" title="Mihajlo Pupin">Mihajlo Pupin</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[286]</a></sup> chief-engineer of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Barclay_Parsons" title="William Barclay Parsons">William Barclay Parsons</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[287]</a></sup> philosophers <a href="/wiki/Irwin_Edman" title="Irwin Edman">Irwin Edman</a><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[288]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Nozick" title="Robert Nozick">Robert Nozick</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[289]</a></sup> economist <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[290]</a></sup> and psychologist <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Babcock" title="Harriet Babcock">Harriet Babcock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[291]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Many Columbia alumni have gone on to renowned careers in the arts, such as the composers <a href="/wiki/Richard_Rodgers" title="Richard Rodgers">Richard Rodgers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[292]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Hammerstein_II" title="Oscar Hammerstein II">Oscar Hammerstein II</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[293]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_Hart" title="Lorenz Hart">Lorenz Hart</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[294]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Art_Garfunkel" title="Art Garfunkel">Art Garfunkel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[295]</a></sup> Four United States <a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Poet Laureate">Poet Laureates</a> received their degrees from Columbia. Columbia alumni have made an indelible mark in the field of American poetry and literature, with such people as <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kerouac" title="Jack Kerouac">Jack Kerouac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allen_Ginsberg" title="Allen Ginsberg">Allen Ginsberg</a>, pioneers of the <a href="/wiki/Beat_Generation" title="Beat Generation">Beat Generation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[296]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Langston_Hughes" title="Langston Hughes">Langston Hughes</a>, a seminal figure in the <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Renaissance" title="Harlem Renaissance">Harlem Renaissance</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[297]</a></sup> all having attended the university. Other notable writers who attended Columbia include authors <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov">Isaac Asimov</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[298]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J.D._Salinger" class="mw-redirect" title="J.D. Salinger">J.D. Salinger</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[299]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Upton_Sinclair" title="Upton Sinclair">Upton Sinclair</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[300]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Danielle_Valore_Evans" title="Danielle Valore Evans">Danielle Valore Evans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[301]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hunter_S._Thompson" title="Hunter S. Thompson">Hunter S. Thompson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[302]</a></sup></p>\n<p>University alumni have also been very prominent in the film industry, with 28 alumni and former students winning a combined 39 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> (as of 2011), second in the world only to <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> (NYU).<sup id="cite_ref-Columbia_Arts_Alumni_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia_Arts_Alumni-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Columbia_University_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia_University-231">[231]</a></sup> Some notable Columbia alumni that have gone on to work in film include directors <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Lumet" title="Sidney Lumet">Sidney Lumet</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/12_Angry_Men_(1957_film)" title="12 Angry Men (1957 film)">12 Angry Men</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[303]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_Bigelow" title="Kathryn Bigelow">Kathryn Bigelow</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Hurt_Locker" title="The Hurt Locker">The Hurt Locker</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[304]</a></sup> screenwriters <a href="/wiki/Howard_Koch_(screenwriter)" class="mw-redirect" title="Howard Koch (screenwriter)">Howard Koch</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Casablanca_(film)" title="Casablanca (film)">Casablanca</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[305]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_L._Mankiewicz" title="Joseph L. Mankiewicz">Joseph L. Mankiewicz</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/All_About_Eve" title="All About Eve">All About Eve</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[306]</a></sup> and actors <a href="/wiki/James_Cagney" title="James Cagney">James Cagney</a><sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[307]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ed_Harris" title="Ed Harris">Ed Harris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[308]</a></sup></p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n<li class=\'gallerycaption\'>Notable Columbia
